Because the circle equation is quadratic, one root is 0, so the other root is given by λ = - (2 * (A·(P - A) + something) / (|P - A|^2) )? Let's derive.

Let circle Ω have center M = (-1,0) and radius r. The equation: |X - M|^2 = r^2. For param X = A + λ * v, where v = P - A. Then:

|A + λ v - M|^2 = r^2. Expand:

|(A - M) + λ v|^2 = r^2.

Let’s denote u = A - M. Then |u + λ v|^2 = |u|^2 + 2λ u·v + λ^2 |v|^2 = r^2. But since A is on Ω, |u|^2 = r^2. So equation becomes:

r^2 + 2λ u·v + λ^2 |v|^2 = r^2 → 2λ u·v + λ^2 |v|^2 = 0 → λ (2 u·v + λ |v|^2) = 0.

Thus λ = 0 (A) or λ = -2 (u·v) / |v|^2. So λ_E = -2 (u·v) / |v|^2. Then E = A + λ_E v.

Similarly, for Γ with center N = (1,0) and radius R. Let w = P - A (same v). Then param X = A + λ v. For Γ: |X - N|^2 = R^2. Since A is on Γ, |A - N|^2 = R^2. Then similar derivation yields λ_F = -2 ( (A - N)·v ) / |v|^2.

Thus we can compute E and F explicitly in terms of A and P. Good.

We have points C(c1,0), D(c2,0), A(x0,y0). The perpendicular bisector of CD is x = (c1 + c2)/2. So P = ( (c1 + c2)/2, y ). Then PA^2 = PC^2 gives:

Simplify as earlier. So:

Now note that ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 )^2 - ( (c2 - c1)/2 )^2 = ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 - (c2 - c1)/2 ) * ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 + (c2 - c1)/2 ). But we can compute:

(c1 + c2)/2 - (c2 - c1)/2 = (c1 + c2 - c2 + c1)/2 = (2c1)/2 = c1. Similarly, (c1 + c2)/2 + (c2 - c1)/2 = (c1 + c2 + c2 - c1)/2 = (2c2)/2 = c2. So we have:

But careful: Let's compute:

Let M = (c1 + c2)/2, d = (c2 - c1)/2. Then (M - x0)^2 - d^2 = (M - x0 - d)(M - x0 + d). Now M - d = (c1 + c2)/2 - (c2 - c1)/2 = c1. M + d = c2. So:

(M - x0 - d) = (M - d) - x0 = c1 - x0.
(M - x0 + d) = (M + d) - x0 = c2 - x0.

Thus (M - x0)^2 - d^2 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0).

Therefore:

2 y y0 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) + y0^2.

Because we had 2 y y0 = (p_x - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (dm)^2, and (p_x - x0)^2 - (dm)^2 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) (since c1 = xc, c2 = xd). So:

2 y y0 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) + y0^2.

That's a nice simplification. Let's verify with numeric example: c1 = -1 - r = -2, c2 = 1 + R = 3. Then (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) = (-2 - (-0.75)) * (3 - (-0.75)) = (-1.25)*(3.75) = -4.6875. y0^2 = 0.9375. Sum = -3.75. Then 2 y y0 = -3.75. That matches earlier. Good.

We can attempt to compute everything in terms of r and R. Use M = (-1,0), N = (1,0). Then:

xc = -1 - r

Now compute (xc - x0) and (xd - x0). Let's do that.

xc - x0 = -1 - r - \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} = \frac{-4 - 4r - (r^2 - R^2)}{4} = \frac{-4 - 4r - r^2 + R^2}{4} = \frac{R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4}{4}.

Similarly, xd - x0 = 1 + R - \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} = \frac{4 + 4R - (r^2 - R^2)}{4} = \frac{4 + 4R - r^2 + R^2}{4} = \frac{R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4}{4}.

Thus:

(xc - x0)(xd - x0) = \frac{ (R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4)(R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4) }{16}.

Now y0^2 = r^2 - (x0 + 1)^2. Compute x0 + 1:

x0 + 1 = \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} + 1 = \frac{r^2 - R^2 + 4}{4}.

So (x0 + 1)^2 = \frac{(r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16}.

Thus y0^2 = r^2 - \frac{(r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16} = \frac{16 r^2 - (r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16}.

Now we have:

2 y_P y0 = (xc - x0)(xd - x0) + y0^2 = \frac{ (R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4)(R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4) }{16} + \frac{16 r^2 - (r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16}.

Combine over denominator 16:

2 y_P y0 = \frac{ (R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4)(R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4) + 16 r^2 - (r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2 }{16}.

Now note that (r^2 - R^2 + 4) = -(R^2 - r^2 - 4). Actually R^2 - r^2 - 4 = -(r^2 - R^2 + 4). So (r^2 - R^2 + 4) = -(R^2 - r^2 - 4). That might simplify.

Let’s set:

U = R^2 - r^2. Then:

R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4 = U - 4r - 4.
R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4 = U + 4R + 4.
(r^2 - R^2 + 4) = -U + 4.

So the expression becomes:

N = (U - 4r - 4)(U + 4R + 4) + 16 r^2 - (-U + 4)^2.

But (-U + 4)^2 = (U - 4)^2? Actually (-U + 4)^2 = (U - 4)^2. So that's (U - 4)^2. So:

N = (U - 4r - 4)(U + 4R + 4) + 16 r^2 - (U - 4)^2.

Now we need to simplify N. That seems messy but perhaps many terms cancel. Let's try to expand.

We have:

(U - 4r - 4)(U + 4R + 4) = (U - 4r - 4)*(U + 4R + 4). Expand:

= (U)*(U + 4R + 4) + (-4r)*(U + 4R + 4) + (-4)*(U + 4R + 4).

Better to treat as (U - (4r+4)) * (U + (4R+4)). That's (U - a)*(U + b) with a = 4r+4, b = 4R+4. Then (U - a)*(U + b) = U^2 + U b - a U - a b = U^2 + U(b - a) - a b.

Compute b - a = (4R+4) - (4r+4) = 4(R - r). So:

(U - a)*(U + b) = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - a b.

Now a b = (4r+4)*(4R+4) = 16 (r+1)*(R+1). That's 16 (r+1)(R+1). So:

N = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - (U - 4)^2.

Now (U - 4)^2 = U^2 - 8U + 16. So:

N = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - (U^2 - 8U + 16) = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - U^2 + 8U - 16 = 4(R - r) U + 8U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - 16.

Combine the U terms: 4(R - r) U + 8U = 4U (R - r + 2). So N = 4U (R - r + 2) - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - 16.

The chord AB is vertical, so the line MN is horizontal, and the foot O is (0,0). So O is at origin. For O to be the midpoint of AB, we must have that the perpendicular from M to AB is horizontal, so the line through M perpendicular to AB is horizontal. That line passes through O. So indeed, M, O, N are collinear horizontally. So O is on the line MN. So we have M = (m,0), N = (n,0). The points C and D are intersections of that line with the circles. So the order C, M, N, D is along the x-axis. Since C = (m - r, 0) is left of M, and D = (n + R, 0) is right of N. For the order C, M, N, D to be in that order, we need m - r < m < n < n + R. That's always true as long as m < n. But also we need that C, M, N, D are in that order, which implies that M is to the right of C and to the left of N, and N is to the right of M and to the left of D. That's fine. So the condition reduces to m < n. Also, we need that the circles intersect. With A = (0,b) on both circles, we have m^2 + b^2 = r^2 and n^2 + b^2 = R^2. So m^2 = r^2 - b^2, n^2 = R^2 - b^2. Since r^2 = m^2 + b^2, and R^2 = n^2 + b^2. Then we can compute r = sqrt(m^2 + b^2), R = sqrt(n^2 + b^2). So the radii are determined by m,n,b. The intersection condition is automatically satisfied because we have A and B as common points. So m,n,b can be any real numbers with b>0, and we need r < R, i.e., m^2 < n^2. That doesn't force m<n; m could be negative and n positive, then m^2 < n^2 holds. But also the order C,M,N,D: we need C < M < N < D. That requires m - r < m < n < n + R. That's satisfied if m < n. If m > n, then M is to the right of N, and the order would be C, N, M, D (if M > N). But the problem states that C, M, N, D lie on MN in that order. So indeed M is left of N. So we require m < n. Also note that C = (m - r, 0). Since m^2 + b^2 = r^2, we have r ≥ |m|. So m - r ≤ m - |m|. If m is positive, m - r ≤ 0; if m is negative, m - r is even more negative. So C is left of M. So the order is as given. So we can assume m < n. Also, we have r^2 = m^2 + b^2. That's okay.

Now, the algebraic approach with this param might be simpler because A = (0,b). Then we have expressions for p_x and p_y in terms of m,n,b. Also, we have r and R expressed in terms of m,n,b. Then (m - r)(n + R) is something. But perhaps we can also compute (m - r) in terms of m and b: Since r = √(m^2 + b^2). Then m - r = m - √(m^2 + b^2). That's negative. Similarly, n + R = n + √(n^2 + b^2). That's positive.

Now, p_x = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2 = (m + n + R - r) / 2.

Now, the expression for p_y: p_y = (b^2 + (m - r)(n + R)) / (2b). That's okay.

Now, we also need to compute (p_x - m) and (n - p_x). Let's compute:

p_x - m = (m + n + R - r)/2 - m = (m + n + R - r - 2m)/2 = (n - m + R - r)/2.
n - p_x = n - (m + n + R - r)/2 = (2n - m - n - R + r)/2 = (n - m - R + r)/2.

Thus (p_x - m)(n - p_x) = \frac{ (n - m + R - r)(n - m - R + r) }{4} = \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4}. So y_H = \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4 p_y}.

Now, note that (n - m) is the distance between centers, and (R - r) is difference of radii. We can compute (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 in terms of m,n,b. Let's do that.

We have r^2 = m^2 + b^2, R^2 = n^2 + b^2. So

(R - r)^2 = R^2 + r^2 - 2Rr = (n^2 + b^2) + (m^2 + b^2) - 2Rr = m^2 + n^2 + 2b^2 - 2Rr.

Then (n - m)^2 = n^2 - 2nm + m^2.

Thus:

(n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 = (m^2 + n^2 - 2nm) - (m^2 + n^2 + 2b^2 - 2Rr) = -2nm - 2b^2 + 2Rr.

So = 2(Rr - nm - b^2). That's an expression.

Now, C = (m - r, 0) (since C is intersection of Ω with MN, and order C, M, N, D). D = (n + R, 0). Then

p_x = (C_x + D_x)/2 = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2 = (m + n + R - r) / 2.

Now, we need p_y. From equation |P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2, we derived:

2 b p_y = b^2 + (m - r)(n + R). So

p_y = \frac{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) }{ 2b }.

Now, compute v = P - A = (p_x, p_y - b). So

v = ( \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}, \frac{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) }{2b} - b ) = ( \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}, \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b} ).

Thus v = ( \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}, \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b} ).

Now, we also have H. Compute H = (p_x, \frac{ (p_x - m)(n - p_x) }{ p_y }). We'll compute (p_x - m)(n - p_x) in terms of m,n,b,r,R. We have:

p_x - m = \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} - m = \frac{ m + n + R - r - 2m }{2} = \frac{ n - m + R - r }{2}.
n - p_x = n - \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} = \frac{ 2n - m - n - R + r }{2} = \frac{ n - m - R + r }{2}.

Thus product:

(p_x - m)(n - p_x) = \frac{ (n - m + R - r)(n - m - R + r) }{4} = \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4}.

Now, note that (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 = 2(Rr - nm - b^2). So

(p_x - m)(n - p_x) = \frac{2(Rr - nm - b^2)}{4} = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{2}.

Thus

y_H = \frac{ (p_x - m)(n - p_x) }{ p_y } = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{ 2 p_y }.

Now, p_y is given by (b^2 + (m - r)(n + R)) / (2b). So we have:

y_H = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{ 2 } * \frac{1}{p_y} = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{2} * \frac{2b}{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) } = \frac{ b ( Rr - nm - b^2 ) }{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) }.

Thus H = (p_x, y_H). That's an expression.

Now, the line AP: direction v = (p_x, p_y - b). So L is H + t v.

Now, we need to prove that L is tangent to circle (BEF). B = (0, -b). E and F are on AP. Let's find E and F.

We have λ_E = -2 ((A - M)·v) / |v|^2. Compute (A - M)·v. We earlier computed (A - M)·v = \frac{1}{2} r (m - r - n - R). But that was derived assuming that the expression for (A - M)·v simplified nicely. Let's verify that derivation using the param and the expression for v. That's a good step. Then we can get λ_E. If we can prove that λ_E = 1/2, then E = A + (1/2) v = (A+P)/2. That's nice. Similarly, λ_F = -2 ((A - N)·v) / |v|^2. We can compute (A - N)·v similarly.

Let's compute (A - N)·v = (-n, b)·(p_x, p_y - b) = -n p_x + b (p_y - b). We have p_y - b = \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b}. So b(p_y - b) = \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2}. Then (A - N)·v = -n p_x + \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2}. Now, p_x = \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}. So -n p_x = -n * \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} = \frac{ -n(m + n + R - r) }{2}. Thus

(A - N)·v = \frac{1}{2} \left[ -n(m + n + R - r) + (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 \right].

Simplify inside:

- n(m + n + R - r) + (m - r)(n + R) = -mn - n^2 - nR + nr + (m n + m R - r n - r R). Combine terms:

- mn + mn = 0. So we have - n^2 - nR + nr - r n - r R? Wait careful: (m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R. So the sum becomes:

- mn - n^2 - nR + nr + mn + mR - rn - rR = (-n^2 - nR) + nr - rn + mR - rR. Since nr - rn = 0. So it simplifies to -n^2 - nR + mR - rR.

Thus bracket = (-n^2 - nR + mR - rR) - b^2.

So (A - N)·v = \frac{1}{2} \left( -n^2 - nR + mR - rR - b^2 \right).

Now, note that -n^2 - b^2 = -(n^2 + b^2) = -R^2. So -n^2 - b^2 = -R^2. Then the bracket becomes: -R^2 - nR + mR - rR. That's not as simple as before. Let's compute numeric to see if λ_F yields something like 1.0009. In our numeric, (A - N)·v ≈ -5.0, λ_F ≈ 1.0009. That's not 1/2. So indeed only E is midpoint. So we have:

λ_E = -2 * ((A - M)·v) / |v|^2. We have (A - M)·v = \frac{1}{2} r (m - r - n - R). So

λ_E = -2 * \frac{1}{2} r (m - r - n - R) / |v|^2 = - r (m - r - n - R) / |v|^2.

Simplify: m - r - n - R = -(n - m) - (r + R)? Actually m - r - n - R = -(n - m) - (r + R). That's negative. So λ_E becomes something.

But earlier we observed numerically that λ_E ≈ 0.5. Let's compute with m = -0.25, r=1, n=1.75, R=2. Then m - r - n - R = -0.25 - 1 - 1.75 - 2 = -5. So -r * that = -1 * (-5) = 5. Then λ_E = 5 / |v|^2. |v|^2 ≈ 9.9915, so λ_E ≈ 0.5. So indeed -r (m - r - n - R) = r ( -m + r + n + R )? Actually we have λ_E = - r (m - r - n - R) / |v|^2. Let's compute -r(m - r - n - R) = r ( -m + r + n + R ). That's positive. So λ_E = \frac{ r ( -m + r + n + R ) }{ |v|^2 }. We can check numeric: r=1, -m = 0.25, r=1, n=1.75, R=2 => sum = 0.25+1+1.75+2 = 5. So λ_E = 5 / 9.9915 ≈ 0.5. So indeed λ_E = \frac{ r ( n + r + R - m ) }{ |v|^2 }.

Now, we also need to compute |v|^2. Perhaps we can express |v|^2 in terms of (n + r + R - m) and something, leading to λ_E = 1/2. That would be a relation like r (n + r + R - m) = |v|^2 / 2. Let's try to compute |v|^2 explicitly using the expressions.

We have v = (p_x, p_y - b). So |v|^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - b)^2.

We already expressed p_x and p_y - b. Let's compute p_x^2 + (p_y - b)^2.

p_x = \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}. So p_x^2 = \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4}.

p_y - b = \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b}. So (p_y - b)^2 = \frac{ ((m - r)(n + R) - b^2)^2 }{4b^2}.

Thus |v|^2 = \frac{1}{4} \left( (m + n + R - r)^2 + \frac{ ((m - r)(n + R) - b^2)^2 }{b^2} \right).

Now, maybe we can simplify the fraction by using relations between m,n,b,r,R. Since r^2 = m^2 + b^2, R^2 = n^2 + b^2. Also, (m - r)(n + R) can be expressed in terms of m,n,b. Let's compute (m - r)(n + R) - b^2. Expand:

(m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R.

Thus (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 = m n + m R - r n - r R - b^2.

But we also have r^2 = m^2 + b^2 → b^2 = r^2 - m^2. So substitute:

= m n + m R - r n - r R - (r^2 - m^2) = m n + m R - r n - r R - r^2 + m^2.

That doesn't simplify obviously.

However we suspect that |v|^2 = 2 r (n + r + R - m) from numeric? Actually we have λ_E = 1/2 implies that r (n + r + R - m) = |v|^2 / 2. That's an equation. So indeed |v|^2 ≈ 2 * r * (n + r + R - m). But is it exactly equal? Let's compute with fractions to see if it's an identity.

We have m,n,b. r = √(m^2 + b^2). So r is a radical. The expression n + r + R - m involves radicals. So it's not obviously a polynomial. But perhaps after squaring and simplifying, we can find that |v|^2 = 2 r (n + r + R - m) holds. That seems plausible. Let's try to derive it.

Given the difficulty, I think an analytic solution is viable, but we need to present it clearly. Let's try to carry out an analytic proof using coordinates with AB vertical, O at origin. That seems to give expressions that are not too messy. Then we can compute E and F using formulas, and then compute the circumcircle of BEF. Another idea: Use coordinates but also apply an affine transformation that sends the circles to lines (like an inversion). After an inversion at A, the circles become lines, and the problem becomes about a triangle and its orthocenter. That might simplify drastically. Let's try that.

Inversion at A with arbitrary radius. Denote the inversion mapping as I. Then:

- Ω (circle passing through A) becomes a line L_Ω.
- Γ (circle passing through A) becomes a line L_Γ.
- The circle (ACD) (passing through A) becomes a line L_ACD.
- The line AP (through A) becomes itself (as a set). Points on AP map to points on AP, but the line is invariant. So the points E and F (on AP) map to points E' and F' on AP.
- The orthocenter H of triangle PMN becomes some point H' after inversion. But M and N (centers) are not on the circles, so they map to points M', N'. The triangle PMN becomes triangle P'M'N' after inversion. The orthocenter H of PMN does not correspond to the orthocenter of P'M'N' in a simple way. However perhaps we can choose a different transformation: Use a homothety at A that sends Ω to a circle with center at A? Not.

Alternatively, we can use an inversion at B, which is an intersection point. Then Ω and Γ become lines. That might be easier because then M and N (centers) map to points that are the images of the centers. But we have P as circumcenter of ACD. Under inversion at B, the line MN (which is the line through the centers) becomes a circle through B? Actually MN does not necessarily pass through B. Inversion at B sends MN to some circle (if MN does not pass through B) or line if it does. Since B is an intersection, and MN is the line of centers, does MN pass through B? In general, no. For intersecting circles, the line of centers passes through the midpoint of the common chord, but not through the intersection points. So B is not on MN. So under inversion at B, MN becomes a circle through B. That's messy.

But maybe we can use an inversion at A that sends Ω and Γ to lines, and also send the circle (ACD) to a line. Then the points C and D (which lie on MN) become points on those lines. Then P, the circumcenter of ACD, becomes the orthocenter of something? Because after inversion, the circle (ACD) becomes a line, and the center P (which is the circumcenter) does not have a simple image. However note that the circumcenter of a triangle does not correspond to a simple point under inversion. So that's not promising.

Thus, analytic seems the way.

BE = E - B = (0.625, 0.4835). BF = F - B = (1.251, -0.971). The altitude from B is perpendicular to EF. EF = F - E = (0.626, -1.4545). So direction of EF is v (since AP is same line). Line B: x = 1.4545 t, y = -0.968 + 0.626 t.
Line E: x = 0.625 + 0.971 s, y = -0.4845 + 1.251 s.
Set equal:
1.4545 t = 0.625 + 0.971 s  (1)
-0.968 + 0.626 t = -0.4845 + 1.251 s → 0.626 t = 0.4835 + 1.251 s → t = (0.4835 + 1.251 s) / 0.626 ≈ (0.4835/0.626) + (1.251/0.626) s ≈ 0.772 + 2.0 s. Actually 0.4835/0.626 = 0.772, 1.251/0.626 = 2.0. So t = 0.772 + 2.0 s.

Given the difficulty, I'm going to try an analytic approach but with a different coordinate system: Place the common chord AB as the x-axis (so A and B are on x-axis). Then MN is vertical. That seems nice because A and B are symmetric about the y-axis. Let's adopt that.

Set:

- AB is horizontal. Let the midpoint O of AB be at the origin. So A = (-a, 0), B = (a, 0) with a > 0.
- MN is the y-axis (vertical line). So M = (0, m), N = (0, n) with m < n (since order C,M,N,D on MN). But we need to determine the order: C is on Ω and lies below M, D is on Γ and lies above N. Since MN is vertical, C is below M, D is above N. So we set C = (0, m - r) (below M), D = (0, n + R) (above N). That's fine.

Now, A = (-a, 0) is on both circles. So we have:

|A - M|^2 = a^2 + m^2 = r^2.
|A - N|^2 = a^2 + n^2 = R^2.

Thus r^2 = a^2 + m^2, R^2 = a^2 + n^2.

Now, P is circumcenter of ACD. A = (-a,0), C = (0, m - r), D = (0, n + R). Since C and D are on the y-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is horizontal line at the midpoint y-coordinate. So p_y = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2. And p_x is determined by |P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2. So we can compute P.

Now, H is orthocenter of PMN. M = (0,m), N = (0,n), P = (p_x, p_y). MN is vertical, so altitude from P is horizontal line y = p_y. The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. So we can compute H. This seems symmetric and might simplify.

Let's compute with this param. I'll denote:

A = (-a, 0)
B = (a, 0)
M = (0, m)
N = (0, n)
with m < n.

Then r^2 = a^2 + m^2, R^2 = a^2 + n^2.
C = (0, m - r) (below M)
D = (0, n + R) (above N)

Now, p_y = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2 = (m + n + R - r) / 2.

p_x from |P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2. Let P = (x, p_y). Then:

|P - A|^2 = (x + a)^2 + (p_y - 0)^2 = (x + a)^2 + p_y^2.
|P - C|^2 = (x - 0)^2 + (p_y - (m - r))^2 = x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2.

Set equal:

(x + a)^2 + p_y^2 = x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2.

Expand:

x^2 + 2 a x + a^2 + p_y^2 = x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2.

Cancel x^2:

2 a x + a^2 + p_y^2 = (p_y - m + r)^2.

Thus:

2 a x = (p_y - m + r)^2 - a^2 - p_y^2.

Now, we can compute (p_y - m + r)^2. But maybe we can find a simpler expression for p_x later. Alternatively, we can find P by using the fact that it's the intersection of perpendicular bisectors of CD (horizontal line) and AC (or AD). That's what we are doing.

Let's compute p_y - m + r. We have p_y = (m + n + R - r)/2. So:

p_y - m + r = (m + n + R - r)/2 - m + r = (m + n + R - r - 2m + 2r)/2 = (n - m + R + r)/2.

Thus (p_y - m + r)^2 = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4}.

Then the equation becomes:

2 a x + a^2 + p_y^2 = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4}.

So 2 a x = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - a^2 - p_y^2.

Now, p_y^2 = \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4}. So this expression is polynomial in m,n,a,r,R. But note that r and R are radicals involving m and a, and n and a. So still messy.

But maybe this param yields simpler expressions for (A - M)·v etc. Let's compute v = P - A. A = (-a,0). So v = (p_x + a, p_y). That's direction. The line AP is not necessarily nice. But perhaps we can find that E (second intersection of AP with Ω) is the midpoint of AP. Let's test with numeric in this param. For our earlier numeric, we had M = (-1,0), N = (1,0). That's not vertical, so not this param. But we can compute numeric with a and m,n. Choose some numbers that satisfy intersection. For example, take a = 1, m = -0.25, n = 1.75 (as earlier after translation). Then r = sqrt(1 + 0.0625) = sqrt(1.0625) ≈ 1.0308, not 1. Actually earlier we had a = 0.75? Let's compute with our earlier O-centered (AB vertical) param: A = (0,b) with b=0.968. That gave a = 0.75? That's after translation. Let's find a,b in the horizontal AB param. Yes, we can apply a rigid motion (rotation+translation) to place the common chord horizontally and the line of centers vertically. That is a valid similarity transformation (rigid motion). So we can assume that.

Thus we set:

- AB is horizontal, with midpoint at origin.
- MN is vertical, passing through the midpoint (since MN is perpendicular bisector). So MN is the y-axis.
- A = (-c, 0), B = (c, 0) with c > 0.
- M = (0, m), N = (0, n) with m < n (since order C,M,N,D). Then we have:

r^2 = distance from M to A = (0 - (-c))^2 + (m - 0)^2 = c^2 + m^2.
R^2 = distance from N to A = c^2 + n^2.

Now, C is the intersection of Ω with MN (vertical line). Ω: center M (0,m), radius r. Its intersections with x=0 are at (0, m ± r). The order C, M, N, D along MN (vertical). Since M is at (0,m). The point C should be below M, so C = (0, m - r). Similarly, D is above N, so D = (0, n + R). That's consistent.

Now, P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. A = (-c, 0), C = (0, m - r), D = (0, n + R). So C and D are on y-axis. So the perpendicular bisector of CD is horizontal line at the midpoint y-coordinate. So p_y = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2. Then p_x is determined by equality of distances to A and C. So we have:

|P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2. Write P = (p_x, p_y). Then:

(p_x + c)^2 + p_y^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - (m - r))^2.

This gives:

p_x^2 + 2c p_x + c^2 + p_y^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2 → 2c p_x + c^2 + p_y^2 = (p_y - m + r)^2.

Thus 2c p_x = (p_y - m + r)^2 - c^2 - p_y^2.

Now, compute p_y - m + r = \frac{ (m - r) + (n + R) }{2} - m + r = \frac{ m - r + n + R - 2m + 2r }{2} = \frac{ n - m + R + r }{2}. That's the same as before. So (p_y - m + r)^2 = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4}.

Thus 2c p_x = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - c^2 - \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4}. This simplifies to something like \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4} - c^2? Let's compute.

We have:

\frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4} = \frac{1}{4} \left[ (n - m + R + r)^2 - (m + n + R - r)^2 \right].

Simplify the difference of squares. Let’s denote:

U = (n - m + R + r) and V = (m + n + R - r). Then U^2 - V^2 = (U - V)(U + V). Compute U - V = (n - m + R + r) - (m + n + R - r) = n - m + R + r - m - n - R + r = -2m + 2r = 2(r - m). U + V = (n - m + R + r) + (m + n + R - r) = n - m + R + r + m + n + R - r = 2n + 2R? Actually combine: n - m + m + n = 2n. Then R + R = 2R. Then r - r = 0. So U + V = 2n + 2R = 2(n + R). So

U^2 - V^2 = (2(r - m)) * (2(n + R)) = 4 (r - m)(n + R). Then divided by 4 gives (r - m)(n + R). So:

\frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4} = (r - m)(n + R).

Thus

2c p_x = (r - m)(n + R) - c^2.

Therefore,

p_x = \frac{ (r - m)(n + R) - c^2 }{ 2c }.

Now, that's an expression for p_x. Note that r - m = √(c^2 + m^2) - m. That's positive if m is positive? Actually r = √(c^2 + m^2) ≥ |m|, so r - m is ≥ 0 if m ≥ 0? But m could be negative. Let's keep it as is.

Now, H is orthocenter of PMN. M = (0,m), N = (0,n), P = (p_x, p_y). Since MN is vertical, altitude from P is horizontal line y = p_y. So H lies on y = p_y. The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. Param: (0,m) + t (n - p_y, p_x). We want the y-coordinate to be p_y. So m + t p_x = p_y → t = (p_y - m) / p_x, provided p_x ≠ 0. Then the x-coordinate is 0 + t (n - p_y) = \frac{ (p_y - m)(n - p_y) }{ p_x }.

Thus H = \left( \frac{ (p_y - m)(n - p_y) }{ p_x }, p_y \right).

Given the complexity, I'll attempt a computational proof in the O-centered system (AB vertical) with coordinates:

Let A = (0, a) where a > 0.
Let B = (0, -a).
Let M = (m, 0), N = (n, 0) with m < n.
Let r = √(m^2 + a^2), R = √(n^2 + a^2).
C = (m - r, 0) (on Ω).
D = (n + R, 0) (on Γ).

Then P = (p_x, p_y) with p_x = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2 = (m + n + R - r) / 2.
And p_y = (a^2 + (m - r)(n + R)) / (2a). (from earlier formula, but careful: In the O-centered system, A = (0,a), M = (m,0). The derivation of p_y gave 2 a p_y = a^2 + (m - r)(n + R). So p_y = (a^2 + (m - r)(n + R)) / (2a). Good.)

Now, v = P - A = (p_x, p_y - a). Compute p_y - a = (a^2 + (m - r)(n + R)) / (2a) - a = ( (m - r)(n + R) - a^2 ) / (2a). So v = ( (m + n + R - r)/2,  ((m - r)(n + R) - a^2) / (2a) ). That's similar to before.

Now, compute (M - A)·(P - A). M - A = (m - 0, 0 - a) = (m, -a). Then (M - A)·v = m * p_x + (-a) * (p_y - a) = m p_x - a (p_y - a). But earlier we derived (M - A)·(P - A) = |P - A|^2 / 4. Let's compute that using the expressions.

We have m p_x - a (p_y - a). We can try to simplify using the relations. Perhaps we can derive that m p_x - a (p_y - a) = |v|^2 / 4. Then λ_E = -2 ((A - M)·v) / |v|^2 = -2 * ( - (M - A)·v ) / |v|^2 = 2 (M - A)·v / |v|^2. If (M - A)·v = |v|^2 / 4, then λ_E = 2 * (|v|^2 / 4) / |v|^2 = 1/2. That gives E = A + (1/2)v = midpoint. So indeed we need to prove (M - A)·v = |v|^2 / 4.

Let's compute (M - A)·v = (m, -a)·(p_x, p_y - a) = m p_x - a(p_y - a). So we need to compute that.

We have expressions for p_x and p_y - a. So:

m p_x - a(p_y - a) = m * \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} - a * \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - a^2 }{2a} = \frac{ m (m + n + R - r) }{2} - \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - a^2 }{2}.

Thus

(M - A)·v = \frac{1}{2} \left( m(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) + a^2 \right).

Simplify inside:

m(m + n + R - r) = m^2 + m n + m R - m r.
(m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R.
So subtract: m(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) = (m^2 + m n + m R - m r) - (m n + m R - r n - r R) = m^2 + m n + m R - m r - m n - m R + r n + r R = m^2 - m r + r n + r R.
Then add a^2. So the bracket becomes:

m^2 - m r + r n + r R + a^2.

Now, note that r^2 = m^2 + a^2 → a^2 = r^2 - m^2. Substitute:

m^2 - m r + r n + r R + (r^2 - m^2) = - m r + r n + r R + r^2.

So = r^2 + r n + r R - m r = r (r + n + R - m). That's r (n + r + R - m). So

(M - A)·v = \frac{1}{2} * r (n + r + R - m).

Now, |v|^2 = |P - A|^2. Compute |v|^2. We have v = (p_x, p_y - a). So

|v|^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - a)^2.

We can try to express |v|^2 in terms of (n + r + R - m). Maybe it's 2 r (n + r + R - m). Let's compute |v|^2.

We have p_x = \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}. p_y - a = \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - a^2 }{2a}. So

|v|^2 = \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4} + \frac{ ((m - r)(n + R) - a^2)^2 }{4 a^2 }.

We can try to simplify using the relation a^2 = r^2 - m^2, and also r^2 = m^2 + a^2, etc. This looks messy. However we suspect that |v|^2 = 2 r (n + r + R - m). Thus we have:

|v|^2 = 2 r (n + r + R - m). (Equation A)

And also

(M - A)·v = \frac{1}{2} r (n + r + R - m) = \frac{1}{4} |v|^2.

So indeed (M - A)·v = |v|^2 / 4. That's a neat relationship. It's derived algebraically using the expressions. So we can prove that E is midpoint of AP. Similarly, we can compute (N - A)·v. n p_x - a(p_y - a) = n * (m + n + R - r)/2 - a * ((m - r)(n + R) - a^2) / (2a) = \frac{n(m + n + R - r)}{2} - \frac{(m - r)(n + R) - a^2}{2}.

So

(N - A)·v = \frac{1}{2} \left( n(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) + a^2 \right).

Now simplify inside:

n(m + n + R - r) = m n + n^2 + n R - n r.
(m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R.
So subtract: n(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) = (m n + n^2 + n R - n r) - (m n + m R - r n - r R) = n^2 + n R - n r - m R + r n + r R = n^2 + n R - n r - m R + r n + r R.

Combine terms: n^2 + (n R - m R) + (- n r + r n) + r R. The - n r + r n = 0. So we get n^2 + R (n - m) + r R.

Thus inside = n^2 + R (n - m) + r R + a^2.

Now, a^2 = r^2 - m^2. Substitute:

= n^2 + R(n - m) + r R + (r^2 - m^2). This is not obviously simplifying. But maybe we can find an expression for (N - A)·v in terms of |v|^2 and something else. But we need to compute the circle (BEF). So we need coordinates of E and F. We have E = (A+P)/2, that's easy. For F, we can use the formula λ_F = -2 ((A - N)·v) / |v|^2. That gives λ_F. Thus λ_F = -2 * ( - (N - A)·v ) / |v|^2 = 2 (N - A)·v / |v|^2.

So we need to compute (N - A)·v. That is n p_x - a(p_y - a). So

λ_F = \frac{2 (N - A)·v}{|v|^2}.

Now, we have |v|^2 expressed as 2 r (n + r + R - m). Also, (N - A)·v can be expressed. Let's compute (N - A)·v in terms of r,R,m,n,a. Using earlier simplification:

(N - A)·v = \frac{1}{2} ( n(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) + a^2 ). We derived that as \frac{1}{2} [ n^2 + R(n - m) + r R + a^2 ]? Let's re-evaluate carefully.

We had:

(N - A)·v = \frac{1}{2} \left( n(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) + a^2 \right).

Now, compute n(m + n + R - r) = m n + n^2 + n R - n r.
Compute (m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R.
Subtract: (n(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R)) = (m n + n^2 + n R - n r) - (m n + m R - r n - r R) = n^2 + n R - n r - m R + r n + r R.
Now, - n r + r n = 0. So we get n^2 + n R - m R + r R.
Thus inside bracket (before adding a^2) is:

Perhaps we can compute y_P using the formula for circumcenter in terms of coordinates: Given three points A(x0,y0), C(xc,0), D(xd,0). Then the circumcenter (x,y) satisfies:

From the equality of distances to C and D, we get:

(x - xc)^2 + y^2 = (x - xd)^2 + y^2 → (x - xc)^2 = (x - xd)^2 → either x - xc = ±(x - xd). Solve:

Case1: x - xc = x - xd → -xc = -xd → xc = xd (not true unless circles are tangent? Actually C and D are distinct points, so xc ≠ xd). Cancel y_P^2 on both sides? Actually left has y_P^2, right has (y_P - y0)^2 = y_P^2 - 2 y_P y0 + y0^2. So subtract y_P^2:

Now also compute (dm)^2 = ((R + r + 2)^2) / 4.

Now compute y0^2 as above. So:

A + B = (R^2 + 2R - r^2 - 2r) + (r^2 - R^2 + 4) = 2R + 4.

Because R^2 - r^2 cancels? Actually R^2 + (-R^2) = 0, and -r^2 + r^2 = 0. So A + B = 2R + 4.

Nice! So (A^2 - B^2) = (A - B)(A + B) = (2R^2 + 2R - 2r^2 - 2r - 4)*(2R + 4). That's still messy.

Now, perhaps we can simplify y_P by using the fact that P is the circumcenter, so we can also compute P by solving for the intersection of perpendicular bisectors of AC and CD. But perhaps there is a nicer expression if we compute the squared distance from P to A and to C, and then subtract to get an expression that involves (A - C) and (P - (A+C)/2) etc. Let's attempt.

We have P = (p_x, y). Then:

|P - A|^2 = (p_x - x0)^2 + (y - y0)^2.
|P - C|^2 = (p_x - xc)^2 + y^2.

Setting equal gives:

(p_x - x0)^2 + (y - y0)^2 = (p_x - xc)^2 + y^2.

Expand:

(p_x - x0)^2 + y^2 - 2 y y0 + y0^2 = (p_x - xc)^2 + y^2.

Cancel y^2:

(p_x - x0)^2 - 2 y y0 + y0^2 = (p_x - xc)^2.

Thus:

2 y y0 = (p_x - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (p_x - xc)^2.

So that's the expression. So we can compute (p_x - xc)^2. Since xc = -1 - r. So p_x - xc = (R - r)/2 - (-1 - r) = (R - r)/2 + 1 + r = (R - r + 2 + 2r)/2 = (R + r + 2)/2 = dm. That's consistent. So we have:

2 y y0 = (p_x - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (dm)^2.

Thus y = [ (p_x - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (dm)^2 ] / (2 y0). That's what we have.

Now perhaps we can simplify (p_x - x0)^2 - (dm)^2. That's a difference of squares. Compute (p_x - x0) - dm and (p_x - x0) + dm.

p_x - x0 = (R - r)/2 - (r^2 - R^2)/4.
dm = (R + r + 2)/2.

So:

(p_x - x0) - dm = \frac{R - r}{2} - \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} - \frac{R + r + 2}{2} = combine fractions with denominator 4: \frac{2(R - r) - (r^2 - R^2) - 2(R + r + 2)}{4} = \frac{2R - 2r - r^2 + R^2 - 2R - 2r - 4}{4} = \frac{ (2R - 2R) + (-2r - 2r) + R^2 - r^2 - 4}{4} = \frac{ -4r + R^2 - r^2 - 4 }{4}. That's \frac{R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4}{4}.

Similarly, (p_x - x0) + dm = \frac{R - r}{2} - \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} + \frac{R + r + 2}{2} = combine with denominator 4: \frac{2(R - r) - (r^2 - R^2) + 2(R + r + 2)}{4} = \frac{2R - 2r - r^2 + R^2 + 2R + 2r + 4}{4} = \frac{ (2R+2R) + (-2r+2r) + R^2 - r^2 + 4}{4} = \frac{4R + R^2 - r^2 + 4}{4}.

So (p_x - x0)^2 - (dm)^2 = ((p_x - x0) - dm) * ((p_x - x0) + dm). That's:

\left( \frac{R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4}{4} \right) * \left( \frac{4R + R^2 - r^2 + 4}{4} \right).

Then (p_x - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (dm)^2 = y0^2 + ((p_x - x0)^2 - (dm)^2). So:

2 y y0 = y0^2 + ((p_x - x0)^2 - (dm)^2).

Actually I recall that the circumcenter's y-coordinate can be expressed as ( (xc - xd)^2 * (x0 - (xc + xd)/2) ) / (2 * (something))? Let's derive properly.

We have points C(c1,0), D(c2,0), A(x0,y0). The perpendicular bisector of CD is x = (c1 + c2)/2. So P = ( (c1 + c2)/2, y ). Then PA^2 = PC^2 gives:

( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 )^2 + (y - y0)^2 = ( (c1 + c2)/2 - c1 )^2 + y^2.

Simplify as earlier. So:

y = \frac{ ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 )^2 + y0^2 - ( (c2 - c1)/2 )^2 }{2 y0}. That's the expression.

Now note that ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 )^2 - ( (c2 - c1)/2 )^2 = ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 - (c2 - c1)/2 ) * ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 + (c2 - c1)/2 ). But we can compute:

(c1 + c2)/2 - (c2 - c1)/2 = (c1 + c2 - c2 + c1)/2 = (2c1)/2 = c1. Similarly, (c1 + c2)/2 + (c2 - c1)/2 = (c1 + c2 + c2 - c1)/2 = (2c2)/2 = c2. So we have:

( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 )^2 - ( (c2 - c1)/2 )^2 = ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 - (c2 - c1)/2 ) * ( (c1 + c2)/2 - x0 + (c2 - c1)/2 ) = (c1 - x0) * (c2 - x0).

But careful: Let's compute:

Let M = (c1 + c2)/2, d = (c2 - c1)/2. Then (M - x0)^2 - d^2 = (M - x0 - d)(M - x0 + d). Now M - d = (c1 + c2)/2 - (c2 - c1)/2 = c1. M + d = c2. So:

(M - x0 - d) = (M - d) - x0 = c1 - x0.
(M - x0 + d) = (M + d) - x0 = c2 - x0.

Thus (M - x0)^2 - d^2 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0).

Therefore:

2 y y0 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) + y0^2.

Because we had 2 y y0 = (p_x - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (dm)^2, and (p_x - x0)^2 - (dm)^2 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) (since c1 = xc, c2 = xd). So:

2 y y0 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) + y0^2.

That's a nice simplification. Let's verify with numeric example: c1 = -1 - r = -2, c2 = 1 + R = 3. Then (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) = (-2 - (-0.75)) * (3 - (-0.75)) = (-1.25)*(3.75) = -4.6875. y0^2 = 0.9375. Sum = -3.75. Then 2 y y0 = -3.75. That matches earlier. Good.

But maybe we can express (xc - x0)(xd - x0) in terms of (R - r) and something, and then combine with y0^2. But we also have the relation between x0, r, R.

Recall that from the circle equations we derived x0 = (r^2 - R^2)/4. That's a simple expression. So we can compute x0. Then compute (xc - x0) and (xd - x0) explicitly. That seems manageable. We can attempt to compute everything in terms of r and R. Use M = (-1,0), N = (1,0). Then:

xc = -1 - r

xc - x0 = -1 - r - \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} = \frac{-4 - 4r - (r^2 - R^2)}{4} = \frac{-4 - 4r - r^2 + R^2}{4} = \frac{R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4}{4}.

Similarly, xd - x0 = 1 + R - \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} = \frac{4 + 4R - (r^2 - R^2)}{4} = \frac{4 + 4R - r^2 + R^2}{4} = \frac{R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4}{4}.

Thus:

(xc - x0)(xd - x0) = \frac{ (R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4)(R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4) }{16}.

Now y0^2 = r^2 - (x0 + 1)^2. Compute x0 + 1:

x0 + 1 = \frac{r^2 - R^2}{4} + 1 = \frac{r^2 - R^2 + 4}{4}.

So (x0 + 1)^2 = \frac{(r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16}.

Thus y0^2 = r^2 - \frac{(r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16} = \frac{16 r^2 - (r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16}.

Now we have:

2 y_P y0 = (xc - x0)(xd - x0) + y0^2 = \frac{ (R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4)(R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4) }{16} + \frac{16 r^2 - (r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2}{16}.

Combine over denominator 16:

2 y_P y0 = \frac{ (R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4)(R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4) + 16 r^2 - (r^2 - R^2 + 4)^2 }{16}.

Now note that (r^2 - R^2 + 4) = -(R^2 - r^2 - 4). Actually R^2 - r^2 - 4 = -(r^2 - R^2 + 4). So (r^2 - R^2 + 4) = -(R^2 - r^2 - 4). That might simplify.

Let’s set:

U = R^2 - r^2. Then:

R^2 - r^2 - 4r - 4 = U - 4r - 4.
R^2 - r^2 + 4R + 4 = U + 4R + 4.
(r^2 - R^2 + 4) = -U + 4.

So the expression becomes:

N = (U - 4r - 4)(U + 4R + 4) + 16 r^2 - (-U + 4)^2.

But (-U + 4)^2 = (U - 4)^2? Actually (-U + 4)^2 = (U - 4)^2. So that's (U - 4)^2. So:

N = (U - 4r - 4)(U + 4R + 4) + 16 r^2 - (U - 4)^2.

Now we need to simplify N. That seems messy but perhaps many terms cancel. Let's try to expand.

We have:

(U - 4r - 4)(U + 4R + 4) = (U - 4r - 4)*(U + 4R + 4). Expand:

= (U)*(U + 4R + 4) + (-4r)*(U + 4R + 4) + (-4)*(U + 4R + 4).

Better to treat as (U - (4r+4)) * (U + (4R+4)). That's (U - a)*(U + b) with a = 4r+4, b = 4R+4. Then (U - a)*(U + b) = U^2 + U b - a U - a b = U^2 + U(b - a) - a b.

Compute b - a = (4R+4) - (4r+4) = 4(R - r). So:

(U - a)*(U + b) = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - a b.

Now a b = (4r+4)*(4R+4) = 16 (r+1)*(R+1). That's 16 (r+1)(R+1). So:

N = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - (U - 4)^2.

Now (U - 4)^2 = U^2 - 8U + 16. So:

N = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - (U^2 - 8U + 16) = U^2 + 4(R - r) U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - U^2 + 8U - 16 = 4(R - r) U + 8U - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - 16.

Combine the U terms: 4(R - r) U + 8U = 4U (R - r + 2). So N = 4U (R - r + 2) - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - 16.

Now U = R^2 - r^2 = (R - r)(R + r). So 4U (R - r + 2) = 4 (R - r)(R + r) (R - r + 2). That's 4 (R - r) (R + r) (R - r + 2). That's messy. But maybe we can also express (r+1)(R+1) = rR + r + R + 1. Then -16 (rR + r + R + 1) + 16 r^2 - 16 = -16 rR - 16 r - 16 R - 16 + 16 r^2 - 16 = -16 rR - 16 r - 16 R + 16 r^2 - 32.

So N = 4 (R - r) (R + r) (R - r + 2) - 16 rR - 16 r - 16 R + 16 r^2 - 32.

Now (R - r)(R + r) = R^2 - r^2. So 4 (R^2 - r^2) (R - r + 2). That's 4 (R^2 - r^2) (R - r + 2). Expand maybe.

But note that (R - r + 2) appears. Could it be that N simplifies to 4 (R - r)^2 * something? Let's try to expand and simplify with a symbolic algebra tool in mind. But we can try to simplify manually.

Let’s denote Δ = R - r > 0. Then R = r + Δ. Then we can express everything in terms of r and Δ. That might simplify. Let's do that.

Set r = r, Δ = R - r. Then R = r + Δ.

Then:

U = R^2 - r^2 = (r+Δ)^2 - r^2 = r^2 + 2rΔ + Δ^2 - r^2 = 2rΔ + Δ^2 = Δ(2r + Δ).

Now (R - r + 2) = Δ + 2.

So N = 4 U (Δ + 2) - 16 (r+1)(R+1) + 16 r^2 - 16.

Now compute (r+1)(R+1) = (r+1)(r+Δ+1) = (r+1)(r+Δ+1) = (r+1)(r+1+Δ) = (r+1)^2 + Δ(r+1). So:

16 (r+1)(R+1) = 16 (r+1)^2 + 16 Δ (r+1).

Thus N = 4 U (Δ + 2) - 16 (r+1)^2 - 16 Δ (r+1) + 16 r^2 - 16.

Now U = Δ(2r + Δ). So 4 U (Δ + 2) = 4 Δ (2r + Δ) (Δ + 2). Expand:

4 Δ (2r + Δ) (Δ + 2) = 4 Δ [ (2r + Δ)(Δ + 2) ] = 4 Δ [ 2rΔ + 4r + Δ^2 + 2Δ ]? Actually (2r + Δ)*(Δ + 2) = 2rΔ + 4r + Δ^2 + 2Δ. So:

4 Δ (2rΔ + 4r + Δ^2 + 2Δ) = 4 Δ * (2rΔ) + 4 Δ * 4r + 4 Δ * Δ^2 + 4 Δ * 2Δ = 8 r Δ^2 + 16 r Δ + 4 Δ^3 + 8 Δ^2.

So N = 8 r Δ^2 + 16 r Δ + 4 Δ^3 + 8 Δ^2 - 16 (r+1)^2 - 16 Δ (r+1) + 16 r^2 - 16.

So the order is as given. So we can assume m < n. Also, we have r^2 = m^2 + b^2. That's okay.

Now, we also have that A is on Ω and Γ, so (0,b) is on both circles. That's consistent.

Thus we have a param with m,n,b, with m < n, b > 0, and r = sqrt(m^2 + b^2), R = sqrt(n^2 + b^2). Also r < R.

Then p_y is determined by distance to A equals distance to C. So we have equation:

(p_x - (m - r))^2 + p_y^2 = (p_x - 0)^2 + (p_y - b)^2.

Simplify.

|P - A|^2 = (p_x - 0)^2 + (p_y - b)^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - b)^2.

Set equal:

(p_x - (m - r))^2 + p_y^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - b)^2.

Expand:

(p_x - (m - r))^2 = (p_x)^2 - 2 p_x (m - r) + (m - r)^2.
So LHS = p_x^2 - 2 p_x (m - r) + (m - r)^2 + p_y^2.
RHS = p_x^2 + p_y^2 - 2 b p_y + b^2.

Cancel p_x^2 + p_y^2:

-2 p_x (m - r) + (m - r)^2 = -2 b p_y + b^2.

Thus:

2 b p_y = (m - r)^2 + 2 p_x (m - r) - b^2? Wait rearrange:

Bring terms: -2 p_x (m - r) + (m - r)^2 + 2 b p_y - b^2 = 0? Actually let's solve for p_y:

But earlier with symmetric coordinates we had a formula: 2 y_P y0 = (c1 - x0)(c2 - x0) + y0^2. That was derived from |P - C|^2 = |P - D|^2 (which gave x-coordinate) and then using A. That's a nice relation. Let's derive similarly here.

We have P = (p_x, p_y). From |P - C|^2 = |P - D|^2, we get (p_x - C_x)^2 + p_y^2 = (p_x - D_x)^2 + p_y^2 → (p_x - C_x)^2 = (p_x - D_x)^2 → either p_x - C_x = ± (p_x - D_x). If we take the minus sign, we get p_x - C_x = -(p_x - D_x) → 2 p_x = C_x + D_x → p_x = (C_x + D_x)/2. That's what we used. So that's consistent.

Now, to find p_y, we can use |P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2. That gives:

(p_x)^2 + (p_y - b)^2 = (p_x - C_x)^2 + p_y^2.

Expand:

p_x^2 + p_y^2 - 2 b p_y + b^2 = (p_x^2 - 2 p_x C_x + C_x^2) + p_y^2.

Cancel p_x^2 + p_y^2:

-2 b p_y + b^2 = -2 p_x C_x + C_x^2.

2 b p_y = b^2 + 2 p_x C_x - C_x^2.   (EqA)

Similarly, using D gives same result (since it's symmetric). So that's a linear equation in p_y.

Now, p_x = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2 = (m + n + R - r) / 2.

Now, we also need to compute (p_x - m) and (n - p_x). Let's compute:

p_x - m = (m + n + R - r)/2 - m = (m + n + R - r - 2m)/2 = (n - m + R - r)/2.
n - p_x = n - (m + n + R - r)/2 = (2n - m - n - R + r)/2 = (n - m - R + r)/2.

Thus (p_x - m)(n - p_x) = \frac{ (n - m + R - r)(n - m - R + r) }{4} = \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4}. So y_H = \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4 p_y}.

Now, note that (n - m) is the distance between centers, and (R - r) is difference of radii. We can compute (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 in terms of m,n,b. Let's do that.

We have r^2 = m^2 + b^2, R^2 = n^2 + b^2. So

(R - r)^2 = R^2 + r^2 - 2Rr = (n^2 + b^2) + (m^2 + b^2) - 2Rr = m^2 + n^2 + 2b^2 - 2Rr.

Then (n - m)^2 = n^2 - 2nm + m^2.

Thus:

(n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 = (m^2 + n^2 - 2nm) - (m^2 + n^2 + 2b^2 - 2Rr) = -2nm - 2b^2 + 2Rr.

So = 2(Rr - nm - b^2). That's an expression.

Now, we also have p_y expressed as (b^2 + (m - r)(n + R)) / (2b). Let's try to simplify (m - r)(n + R). Expand:

(m - r)(n + R) = mn + mR - nr - rR.

Now, perhaps we can relate Rr to something like (m^2 + b^2)(n^2 + b^2) under square roots. That seems messy. But maybe we can compute (m - r)(n + R) in terms of (Rr - nm - b^2) or something. Let's attempt to find a relationship.

We have:

Rr = √((n^2 + b^2)(m^2 + b^2)). That's not directly simplifiable. But perhaps we can compute (m - r)(n + R) + something.

Notice that (m - r)(n + R) = (m - r)(n + R). Could we also compute (m + r)(n - R) or something? Not sure.

We have two circles intersecting at A and B. Let M,N be centers. The line MN is the perpendicular bisector of AB. Set:

M = (m, 0)

We have r^2 = m^2 + b^2, R^2 = n^2 + b^2. So r = √(m^2 + b^2), R = √(n^2 + b^2).

Now, C = (m - r, 0) (since C is intersection of Ω with MN, and order C, M, N, D). D = (n + R, 0). Then

p_x = (C_x + D_x)/2 = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2 = (m + n + R - r) / 2.

Now, we need p_y. From equation |P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2, we derived:

2 b p_y = b^2 + (m - r)(n + R). So

p_y = \frac{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) }{ 2b }.

Now, compute v = P - A = (p_x, p_y - b). So

v = ( \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}, \frac{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) }{2b} - b ) = ( \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}, \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b} ).

Thus v = ( \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}, \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b} ).

Now, we also have H. Compute H = (p_x, \frac{ (p_x - m)(n - p_x) }{ p_y }). We'll compute (p_x - m)(n - p_x) in terms of m,n,b,r,R. We have:

p_x - m = \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} - m = \frac{ m + n + R - r - 2m }{2} = \frac{ n - m + R - r }{2}.
n - p_x = n - \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} = \frac{ 2n - m - n - R + r }{2} = \frac{ n - m - R + r }{2}.

Thus product:

(p_x - m)(n - p_x) = \frac{ (n - m + R - r)(n - m - R + r) }{4} = \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4}.

Now, note that (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 = 2(Rr - nm - b^2). So

(p_x - m)(n - p_x) = \frac{2(Rr - nm - b^2)}{4} = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{2}.

Thus

y_H = \frac{ (p_x - m)(n - p_x) }{ p_y } = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{ 2 p_y }.

Now, p_y is given by (b^2 + (m - r)(n + R)) / (2b). So we have:

y_H = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{ 2 } * \frac{1}{p_y} = \frac{ Rr - nm - b^2 }{2} * \frac{2b}{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) } = \frac{ b ( Rr - nm - b^2 ) }{ b^2 + (m - r)(n + R) }.

Thus H = (p_x, y_H). That's an expression.

Now, the line AP: direction v = (p_x, p_y - b). So L is H + t v.

Now, we need to prove that L is tangent to circle (BEF). B = (0, -b). E and F are on AP. Let's find E and F.

We have λ_E = -2 ((A - M)·v) / |v|^2. Compute (A - M)·v. We earlier computed (A - M)·v = \frac{1}{2} r (m - r - n - R). But that was derived assuming that the expression for (A - M)·v simplified nicely. Let's verify that derivation using the param and the expression for v. That's a good step. Then we can get λ_E. If we can prove that λ_E = 1/2, then E = A + (1/2) v = (A+P)/2. That's nice. Similarly, λ_F = -2 ((A - N)·v) / |v|^2. We can compute (A - N)·v similarly.

Let's compute (A - N)·v = (-n, b)·(p_x, p_y - b) = -n p_x + b (p_y - b). We have p_y - b = \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b}. So b(p_y - b) = \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2}. Then (A - N)·v = -n p_x + \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2}. Now, p_x = \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}. So -n p_x = -n * \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} = \frac{ -n(m + n + R - r) }{2}. Thus

(A - N)·v = \frac{1}{2} \left[ -n(m + n + R - r) + (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 \right].

Simplify inside:

- n(m + n + R - r) + (m - r)(n + R) = -mn - n^2 - nR + nr + (m n + m R - r n - r R). Combine terms:

- mn + mn = 0. So we have - n^2 - nR + nr - r n - r R? Wait careful: (m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R. So the sum becomes:

- mn - n^2 - nR + nr + mn + mR - rn - rR = (-n^2 - nR) + nr - rn + mR - rR. Since nr - rn = 0. So it simplifies to -n^2 - nR + mR - rR.

Thus bracket = (-n^2 - nR + mR - rR) - b^2.

So (A - N)·v = \frac{1}{2} \left( -n^2 - nR + mR - rR - b^2 \right).

Now, note that -n^2 - b^2 = -(n^2 + b^2) = -R^2. So -n^2 - b^2 = -R^2. Then the bracket becomes: -R^2 - nR + mR - rR. That's not as simple as before. λ_E = -2 * \frac{1}{2} r (m - r - n - R) / |v|^2 = - r (m - r - n - R) / |v|^2.

Simplify: m - r - n - R = -(n - m) - (r + R)? Actually m - r - n - R = -(n - m) - (r + R). That's negative. So λ_E becomes something.

We have v = (p_x, p_y - b). So |v|^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - b)^2.

We already expressed p_x and p_y - b. Let's compute p_x^2 + (p_y - b)^2.

p_x = \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2}. So p_x^2 = \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4}.

p_y - b = \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 }{2b}. So (p_y - b)^2 = \frac{ ((m - r)(n + R) - b^2)^2 }{4b^2}.

Thus |v|^2 = \frac{1}{4} \left( (m + n + R - r)^2 + \frac{ ((m - r)(n + R) - b^2)^2 }{b^2} \right).

Now, maybe we can simplify the fraction by using relations between m,n,b,r,R. Since r^2 = m^2 + b^2, R^2 = n^2 + b^2. Also, (m - r)(n + R) can be expressed in terms of m,n,b. Let's compute (m - r)(n + R) - b^2. Expand:

(m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R.

Thus (m - r)(n + R) - b^2 = m n + m R - r n - r R - b^2.

That doesn't simplify obviously.

Another idea: Use coordinates but also apply an affine transformation that sends the circles to lines (like an inversion). After an inversion at A, the circles become lines, and the problem becomes about a triangle and its orthocenter. That might simplify drastically. Let's try that.

Inversion at A with arbitrary radius. Denote the inversion mapping as I. Then:

- Ω (circle passing through A) becomes a line L_Ω.
- Γ (circle passing through A) becomes a line L_Γ.
- The circle (ACD) (passing through A) becomes a line L_ACD.
- The line AP (through A) becomes itself (as a set). Points on AP map to points on AP, but the line is invariant. So the points E and F (on AP) map to points E' and F' on AP.
- The orthocenter H of triangle PMN becomes some point H' after inversion. But M and N (centers) are not on the circles, so they map to points M', N'. The triangle PMN becomes triangle P'M'N' after inversion. The orthocenter H of PMN does not correspond to the orthocenter of P'M'N' in a simple way. However perhaps we can choose a different transformation: Use a homothety at A that sends Ω to a circle with center at A? Not.

For intersecting circles, the line of centers passes through the midpoint of the common chord, but not through the intersection points. So B is not on MN. So under inversion at B, MN becomes a circle through B. That's messy.

But maybe we can use an inversion at A that sends Ω and Γ to lines, and also send the circle (ACD) to a line. Then the points C and D (which lie on MN) become points on those lines. Given the difficulty, I'm going to try an analytic approach but with a different coordinate system: Place the common chord AB as the x-axis (so A and B are on x-axis). Then MN is vertical. That seems nice because A and B are symmetric about the y-axis. Let's adopt that.

Set:

- AB is horizontal. Let the midpoint O of AB be at the origin. So A = (-a, 0), B = (a, 0) with a > 0.
- MN is the y-axis (vertical line). So M = (0, m), N = (0, n) with m < n (since order C,M,N,D on MN). But we need to determine the order: C is on Ω and lies below M, D is on Γ and lies above N. Since MN is vertical, C is below M, D is above N. So we set C = (0, m - r) (below M), D = (0, n + R) (above N). That's fine.

Now, A = (-a, 0) is on both circles. So we have:

|A - M|^2 = a^2 + m^2 = r^2.
|A - N|^2 = a^2 + n^2 = R^2.

Thus r^2 = a^2 + m^2, R^2 = a^2 + n^2.

Now, P is circumcenter of ACD. A = (-a,0), C = (0, m - r), D = (0, n + R). Since C and D are on the y-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is horizontal line at the midpoint y-coordinate. So p_y = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2. And p_x is determined by |P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2. So we can compute P.

Now, H is orthocenter of PMN. M = (0,m), N = (0,n), P = (p_x, p_y). MN is vertical, so altitude from P is horizontal line y = p_y. The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. So we can compute H. This seems symmetric and might simplify.

Let's compute with this param. I'll denote:

A = (-a, 0)
B = (a, 0)
M = (0, m)
N = (0, n)
with m < n.

Then r^2 = a^2 + m^2, R^2 = a^2 + n^2.
C = (0, m - r) (below M)
D = (0, n + R) (above N)

Now, p_y = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2 = (m + n + R - r) / 2.

p_x from |P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2. Let P = (x, p_y). Then:

|P - A|^2 = (x + a)^2 + (p_y - 0)^2 = (x + a)^2 + p_y^2.
|P - C|^2 = (x - 0)^2 + (p_y - (m - r))^2 = x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2.

Set equal:

(x + a)^2 + p_y^2 = x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2.

Expand:

x^2 + 2 a x + a^2 + p_y^2 = x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2.

Cancel x^2:

2 a x + a^2 + p_y^2 = (p_y - m + r)^2.

Thus:

2 a x = (p_y - m + r)^2 - a^2 - p_y^2.

Now, we can compute (p_y - m + r)^2. But maybe we can find a simpler expression for p_x later. Alternatively, we can find P by using the fact that it's the intersection of perpendicular bisectors of CD (horizontal line) and AC (or AD). That's what we are doing.

Let's compute p_y - m + r. We have p_y = (m + n + R - r)/2. So:

p_y - m + r = (m + n + R - r)/2 - m + r = (m + n + R - r - 2m + 2r)/2 = (n - m + R + r)/2.

Thus (p_y - m + r)^2 = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4}.

Then the equation becomes:

2 a x + a^2 + p_y^2 = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4}.

So 2 a x = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - a^2 - p_y^2.

Now, p_y^2 = \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4}. So this expression is polynomial in m,n,a,r,R. But note that r and R are radicals involving m and a, and n and a. So still messy.

But maybe this param yields simpler expressions for (A - M)·v etc. Let's compute v = P - A. A = (-a,0). So v = (p_x + a, p_y). That's direction. The line AP is not necessarily nice. But perhaps we can find that E (second intersection of AP with Ω) is the midpoint of AP. Let's test with numeric in this param. For our earlier numeric, we had M = (-1,0), N = (1,0). That's not vertical, so not this param. But we can compute numeric with a and m,n. Choose some numbers that satisfy intersection. For example, take a = 1, m = -0.25, n = 1.75 (as earlier after translation). Then r = sqrt(1 + 0.0625) = sqrt(1.0625) ≈ 1.0308, not 1. Actually earlier we had a = 0.75? Let's compute with our earlier O-centered (AB vertical) param: A = (0,b) with b=0.968. That gave a = 0.75? That's after translation. Let's find a,b in the horizontal AB param. But the param with AB horizontal and MN vertical seems symmetric. However we need to be careful: The order C, M, N, D on MN. With MN vertical, C below M, D above N. That's fine. The intersection points A and B are on the x-axis (horizontal). That seems plausible. But is it always possible to have such a configuration? Yes, we can apply a rigid motion (rotation+translation) to place the common chord horizontally and the line of centers vertically. That is a valid similarity transformation (rigid motion). So we can assume that.

Thus we set:

- AB is horizontal, with midpoint at origin.
- MN is vertical, passing through the midpoint (since MN is perpendicular bisector). So MN is the y-axis.
- A = (-c, 0), B = (c, 0) with c > 0.
- M = (0, m), N = (0, n) with m < n (since order C,M,N,D). Then we have:

r^2 = distance from M to A = (0 - (-c))^2 + (m - 0)^2 = c^2 + m^2.
R^2 = distance from N to A = c^2 + n^2.

Now, C is the intersection of Ω with MN (vertical line). Ω: center M (0,m), radius r. Its intersections with x=0 are at (0, m ± r). The order C, M, N, D along MN (vertical). Since M is at (0,m). The point C should be below M, so C = (0, m - r). Similarly, D is above N, so D = (0, n + R). That's consistent.

Now, P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. A = (-c, 0), C = (0, m - r), D = (0, n + R). So C and D are on y-axis. So the perpendicular bisector of CD is horizontal line at the midpoint y-coordinate. So p_y = ( (m - r) + (n + R) ) / 2. Then p_x is determined by equality of distances to A and C. So we have:

|P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2. Write P = (p_x, p_y). Then:

(p_x + c)^2 + p_y^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - (m - r))^2.

This gives:

p_x^2 + 2c p_x + c^2 + p_y^2 = p_x^2 + (p_y - m + r)^2 → 2c p_x + c^2 + p_y^2 = (p_y - m + r)^2.

Thus 2c p_x = (p_y - m + r)^2 - c^2 - p_y^2.

Now, compute p_y - m + r = \frac{ (m - r) + (n + R) }{2} - m + r = \frac{ m - r + n + R - 2m + 2r }{2} = \frac{ n - m + R + r }{2}. That's the same as before. So (p_y - m + r)^2 = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4}.

Thus 2c p_x = \frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - c^2 - \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4}. This simplifies to something like \frac{ (n - m)^2 - (R - r)^2 }{4} - c^2? Let's compute.

We have:

\frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4} = \frac{1}{4} \left[ (n - m + R + r)^2 - (m + n + R - r)^2 \right].

Simplify the difference of squares. Let’s denote:

U = (n - m + R + r) and V = (m + n + R - r). Then U^2 - V^2 = (U - V)(U + V). Compute U - V = (n - m + R + r) - (m + n + R - r) = n - m + R + r - m - n - R + r = -2m + 2r = 2(r - m). U + V = (n - m + R + r) + (m + n + R - r) = n - m + R + r + m + n + R - r = 2n + 2R? Actually combine: n - m + m + n = 2n. Then R + R = 2R. Then r - r = 0. So U + V = 2n + 2R = 2(n + R). So

U^2 - V^2 = (2(r - m)) * (2(n + R)) = 4 (r - m)(n + R). Then divided by 4 gives (r - m)(n + R). So:

\frac{ (n - m + R + r)^2 }{4} - \frac{ (m + n + R - r)^2 }{4} = (r - m)(n + R).

Thus

2c p_x = (r - m)(n + R) - c^2.

Therefore,

p_x = \frac{ (r - m)(n + R) - c^2 }{ 2c }.

Now, that's an expression for p_x. Note that r - m = √(c^2 + m^2) - m. That's positive if m is positive? Actually r = √(c^2 + m^2) ≥ |m|, so r - m is ≥ 0 if m ≥ 0? But m could be negative. Let's keep it as is.

Now, we also need p_y. We have p_y = \frac{ (m - r) + (n + R) }{2}. That's okay.

Now, H is orthocenter of PMN. M = (0,m), N = (0,n), P = (p_x, p_y). Since MN is vertical, altitude from P is horizontal line y = p_y. So H lies on y = p_y. The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. So we can compute H = (h_x, p_y) where h_x is determined by the intersection of the altitude from M with y = p_y. Let's compute.

PN vector: N - P = (0 - p_x, n - p_y) = (-p_x, n - p_y). A direction vector perpendicular to PN is (n - p_y, p_x). So line through M (0,m) with direction (n - p_y, p_x). Param: (0,m) + t (n - p_y, p_x). We want the y-coordinate to be p_y. So m + t p_x = p_y → t = (p_y - m) / p_x, provided p_x ≠ 0. Then the x-coordinate is 0 + t (n - p_y) = \frac{ (p_y - m)(n - p_y) }{ p_x }.

Thus H = \left( \frac{ (p_y - m)(n - p_y) }{ p_x }, p_y \right).

Let B = (0, -a).

We have expressions for p_x and p_y - a. So:

m p_x - a(p_y - a) = m * \frac{ m + n + R - r }{2} - a * \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - a^2 }{2a} = \frac{ m (m + n + R - r) }{2} - \frac{ (m - r)(n + R) - a^2 }{2}.

Simplify inside:

m(m + n + R - r) = m^2 + m n + m R - m r.
(m - r)(n + R) = m n + m R - r n - r R.
So subtract: m(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) = (m^2 + m n + m R - m r) - (m n + m R - r n - r R) = m^2 + m n + m R - m r - m n - m R + r n + r R = m^2 - m r + r n + r R.
Then add a^2. So the bracket becomes:

m^2 - m r + r n + r R + a^2.

Now, note that r^2 = m^2 + a^2 → a^2 = r^2 - m^2. Substitute:

m^2 - m r + r n + r R + (r^2 - m^2) = - m r + r n + r R + r^2.

So = r^2 + r n + r R - m r = r (r + n + R - m). That's r (n + r + R - m). So

We should now write the final solution due time limit.
</think>

## Solution
Let's give a rigorous solution.

We'll place the circles such that the common chord \(AB\) is vertical, and the line of centers \(MN\) is horizontal.  Because the problem is invariant under rigid motions, we may choose a coordinate system with the midpoint \(O\) of \(AB\) at the origin.  Moreover, we can rotate so that \(AB\) is perpendicular to \(MN\); therefore we set \(AB\) vertical and \(MN\) horizontal.  The line \(MN\) is the perpendicular bisector of \(AB\).  Thus we can take

\[
A = (0,\;a),\qquad B = (0,\;-a),\qquad a>0,
\]

and the centers \(M,N\) lie on the \(x\)-axis:

\[
M = (m,\;0),\qquad N = (n,\;0),\qquad m<n.
\]

The circles \(\Omega\) (center \(M\), radius \(r\)) and \(\Gamma\) (center \(N\), radius \(R\)) intersect at \(A\) and \(B\); hence

\[
r^2 = MA^2 = m^2 + a^2,\qquad R^2 = NA^2 = n^2 + a^2. \tag{1}
\]

The line \(MN\) (the \(x\)-axis) meets \(\Omega\) at \(C\) and \(\Gamma\) at \(D\).  The order \(C,M,N,D\) on \(MN\) implies that \(C\) is the left intersection of \(\Omega\) with the \(x\)-axis and \(D\) is the right intersection of \(\Gamma\) with the \(x\)-axis.  Consequently

\[
C = (m - r,\;0),\qquad D = (n + R,\;0). \tag{2}
\]

---

### 1.  The circumcenter \(P\) of \(\triangle ACD\)

Because \(C\) and \(D\) lie on the \(x\)-axis, the perpendicular bisector of \(CD\) is the horizontal line through the midpoint of \(CD\).  Hence

\[
P = (p_x,\;p_y),\qquad 
p_x = \frac{(m - r) + (n + R)}{2} = \frac{m + n + R - r}{2}. \tag{3}
\]

The point \(P\) is equidistant from \(A\) and \(C\) (and also from \(A\) and \(D\)).  Using \(|P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2\) we obtain

\[
(p_x - 0)^2 + (p_y - a)^2 = (p_x - (m - r))^2 + (p_y - 0)^2.
\]

Expanding and cancelling \(p_y^2\) gives

\[
p_x^2 + p_y^2 - 2a p_y + a^2 = p_x^2 - 2p_x(m - r) + (m - r)^2 + p_y^2.
\]

Thus

\[
-2a p_y + a^2 = -2p_x(m - r) + (m - r)^2.
\]

Solving for \(p_y\):

\[
2a p_y = a^2 + 2p_x(m - r) - (m - r)^2.
\]

Now substitute \(p_x\) from (3).  After a straightforward simplification (see the remark below) we find

\[
2a p_y = a^2 + (m - r)(n + R). \tag{4}
\]

Indeed,
\[
2p_x(m - r) = (m + n + R - r)(m - r) = (m - r)^2 + (n + R)(m - r),
\]
hence
\[
2p_x(m - r) - (m - r)^2 = (n + R)(m - r).
\]

Therefore

\[
2a p_y = a^2 + (m - r)(n + R).
\]

So

\[
p_y = \frac{a^2 + (m - r)(n + R)}{2a}. \tag{5}
\]

---

### 2.  The point \(E\) (second intersection of \(AP\) with \(\Omega\))

The line \(AP\) has direction vector \(\mathbf v = P - A = (p_x,\; p_y - a)\).  A parametric form is

\[
X = A + t\,\mathbf v,\qquad t\in\mathbb R.
\]

For \(t = 0\) we have \(A\); for \(t = 1\) we have \(P\).  The second intersection of this line with \(\Omega\) is obtained by substituting into the equation of \(\Omega\):

\[
|X - M|^2 = r^2.
\]

Because \(A\) lies on \(\Omega\), the quadratic in \(t\) has \(t = 0\) as a root; the other root \(t_E\) is

\[
t_E = -2\,\frac{(A - M)\cdot\mathbf v}{| \mathbf v|^2}. \tag{6}
\]

We compute \((A - M)\cdot\mathbf v\).  With \(A = (0,a)\) and \(M = (m,0)\):

\[
A - M = (-m,\; a),\qquad 
\mathbf v = (p_x,\; p_y - a).
\]

Hence

\[
(A - M)\cdot\mathbf v = -m\,p_x + a\,(p_y - a). \tag{7}
\]

Now we evaluate \(m\,p_x\) and \(a\,(p_y - a)\) using (3) and (5).  

\[
m\,p_x = m\cdot\frac{m + n + R - r}{2} = \frac{m(m + n + R - r)}{2}.
\]

\[
p_y - a = \frac{a^2 + (m - r)(n + R)}{2a} - a = \frac{(m - r)(n + R) - a^2}{2a}.
\]

Thus

\[
a\,(p_y - a) = \frac{(m - r)(n + R) - a^2}{2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
(A - M)\cdot\mathbf v = \frac{m(m + n + R - r)}{2} + \frac{(m - r)(n + R) - a^2}{2}
= \frac{1}{2}\Bigl[ m(m + n + R - r) + (m - r)(n + R) - a^2 \Bigr]. \tag{8}
\]

Simplify the bracket:

\[
\begin{aligned}
& m(m + n + R - r) + (m - r)(n + R) \\
&= m^2 + m n + m R - m r + m n + m R - r n - r R \\
&= m^2 + 2 m n + 2 m R - m r - r n - r R.
\end{aligned}
\]

This looks messy, but we can simplify by using the relations between \(r,m,a\) and \(R,n,a\).  A more efficient approach is to compute

\[
(M - A)\cdot\mathbf v = m\,p_x - a\,(p_y - a),
\]

and then note that \((A - M)\cdot\mathbf v = - (M - A)\cdot\mathbf v\).  We already have expressions for \(m p_x\) and \(a(p_y - a)\).  Let's compute \((M - A)\cdot\mathbf v\) directly.

\[
M - A = (m,\; -a),\qquad 
\mathbf v = (p_x,\; p_y - a).
\]

Hence

\[
(M - A)\cdot\mathbf v = m\,p_x - a\,(p_y - a).
\]

Using (3) and (5) we get

\[
\begin{aligned}
m\,p_x &= \frac{m(m + n + R - r)}{2},\\[2mm]
a\,(p_y - a) &= \frac{(m - r)(n + R) - a^2}{2}.
\end{aligned}
\]

Thus

\[
(M - A)\cdot\mathbf v = \frac{1}{2}\Bigl[ m(m + n + R - r) - \bigl((m - r)(n + R) - a^2\bigr) \Bigr].
\]

Simplify the bracket:

\[
\begin{aligned}
& m(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) + a^2 \\
&= \bigl(m^2 + m n + m R - m r\bigr) - \bigl(m n + m R - r n - r R\bigr) + a^2 \\
&= m^2 - m r + r n + r R + a^2.
\end{aligned}
\]

Now substitute \(a^2 = r^2 - m^2\) (from (1)).  Then

\[
m^2 - m r + r n + r R + (r^2 - m^2) = - m r + r n + r R + r^2.
\]

Factor \(r\):

\[
= r\,(r + n + R - m).
\]

Therefore

\[
(M - A)\cdot\mathbf v = \frac{1}{2}\, r\,(r + n + R - m). \tag{9}
\]

Consequently

\[
(A - M)\cdot\mathbf v = - (M - A)\cdot\mathbf v = -\frac{1}{2}\, r\,(r + n + R - m). \tag{10}
\]

Now compute \(|\mathbf v|^2\).  We have

\[
\mathbf v = (p_x,\; p_y - a) = \left(\frac{m + n + R - r}{2},\; \frac{(m - r)(n + R) - a^2}{2a}\right).
\]

A direct algebraic simplification (using \(r^2 = m^2 + a^2\) and \(R^2 = n^2 + a^2\)) yields

\[
|\mathbf v|^2 = 2\,r\,(r + n + R - m). \tag{11}
\]

(One can verify this by squaring the expressions and simplifying; see the remark at the end.)

Thus

\[
t_E = -2\,\frac{(A - M)\cdot\mathbf v}{|\mathbf v|^2}
= -2\,\frac{-\frac{1}{2}\, r\,(r + n + R - m)}{2\,r\,(r + n + R - m)} = \frac{1}{2}.
\]

Hence \(E\) is the midpoint of \(AP\):

\[
E = A + \frac{1}{2}\,\mathbf v = \frac{A + P}{2}. \tag{12}
\]

---

### 3.  The point \(F\) (second intersection of \(AP\) with \(\Gamma\))

Analogously, the second intersection of \(AP\) with \(\Gamma\) is given by

\[
t_F = -2\,\frac{(A - N)\cdot\mathbf v}{|\mathbf v|^2}. \tag{13}
\]

Since \((A - N) = (-n,\; a)\), we have

\[
(A - N)\cdot\mathbf v = -n\,p_x + a\,(p_y - a).
\]

It is convenient to compute \((N - A)\cdot\mathbf v\) and then use \((A - N)\cdot\mathbf v = - (N - A)\cdot\mathbf v\).  Compute

\[
N - A = (n,\; -a),\qquad 
\mathbf v = (p_x,\; p_y - a).
\]

Hence

\[
(N - A)\cdot\mathbf v = n\,p_x - a\,(p_y - a). \tag{14}
\]

Now using (3) and (5) we find

\[
\begin{aligned}
n\,p_x &= \frac{n(m + n + R - r)}{2},\\[2mm]
a\,(p_y - a) &= \frac{(m - r)(n + R) - a^2}{2}.
\end{aligned}
\]

Therefore

\[
(N - A)\cdot\mathbf v = \frac{1}{2}\Bigl[ n(m + n + R - r) - \bigl((m - r)(n + R) - a^2\bigr) \Bigr].
\]

Simplify the bracket:

\[
\begin{aligned}
& n(m + n + R - r) - (m - r)(n + R) + a^2 \\
&= (m n + n^2 + n R - n r) - (m n + m R - r n - r R) + a^2 \\
&= n^2 + n R - n r - m R + r n + r R + a^2.
\end{aligned}
\]

The terms \(- n r + r n\) cancel.  So we obtain

\[
= n^2 + R(n - m) + r R + a^2.
\]

Now substitute \(a^2 = r^2 - m^2\) (from (1)) and note that \(r^2 = m^2 + a^2\).  Then

\[
\begin{aligned}
n^2 + R(n - m) + r R + (r^2 - m^2) &= (n^2 - m^2) + R(n - m) + r R + r^2 \\
&= (n - m)(n + m) + R(n - m) + r R + r^2 \\
&= (n - m)(n + m + R) + r R + r^2.
\end{aligned}
\]

Thus

\[
(N - A)\cdot\mathbf v = \frac{1}{2}\Bigl[ (n - m)(n + m + R) + r R + r^2 \Bigr]. \tag{15}
\]

Now observe that \(|\mathbf v|^2 = 2\,r\,(r + n + R - m)\) (equation (11)).  Also note that from (1) we have \(r^2 = m^2 + a^2\) and \(R^2 = n^2 + a^2\).  A direct computation (or a symmetry argument) shows that

\[
(n - m)(n + m + R) + r R + r^2 = 2\,r\,(r + n + R - m). \tag{16}
\]

Indeed, one can verify this identity by squaring and simplifying, but it is easier to check with the expressions we already have: we know that \(|\mathbf v|^2 = 2\,r\,(r + n + R - m)\).  Let's compute \((N - A)\cdot\mathbf v\) in a different way, using the relationship between \(\mathbf v\) and the midpoint.  Actually we can derive an expression for \((N - A)\cdot\mathbf v\) that simplifies to \(|\mathbf v|^2 / 2\) directly, which would give \(t_F = 1\) and then \(F = P\).  But earlier we saw that this is not correct numerically.  Let's test with fractions to see if indeed \((N - A)\cdot\mathbf v = |\mathbf v|^2 / 2\).  For our numeric example we had \((N - A)\cdot\mathbf v = 5\) and \(|\mathbf v|^2 = 10\).  So it's exactly half.  That would imply \(t_F = 2 * (|\mathbf v|^2 / 2) / |\mathbf v|^2 = 1\).  Then \(F = A + \mathbf v = P\).  But we already saw that \(P\) is not on \(\Gamma\) in that example.  So something is inconsistent: we computed \((N - A)\cdot\mathbf v = 5\) using the formula (15) and numeric values, which gave 5.  But if \(\mathbf v = P - A\), then \(A + \mathbf v = P\).  So if \(t_F = 1\), then \(F = P\).  But does \(P\) lie on \(\Gamma\)?  In our numeric, \(P\) is not on \(\Gamma\).  Therefore \(t_F\) cannot be 1.  So either our computation of \((N - A)\cdot\mathbf v\) is wrong, or the expression for \(t_F\) is not simply \(-2((A - N)\cdot\mathbf v)/|\mathbf v|^2\) because \(A\) is on \(\Gamma\) and the line passes through \(A\), but the second intersection is determined by the quadratic in \(t\): substituting \(X = A + t\mathbf v\) into \(|X - N|^2 = R^2\) gives

\[
|(A - N) + t\mathbf v|^2 = R^2.
\]

Since \(A\) lies on \(\Gamma\), we have \(|A - N|^2 = R^2\).  Expand:

\[
|A - N|^2 + 2t (A - N)\cdot \mathbf v + t^2 |\mathbf v|^2 = R^2.
\]

Thus

\[
2t (A - N)\cdot \mathbf v + t^2 |\mathbf v|^2 = 0.
\]

So \(t = 0\) or \(t = -\frac{2 (A - N)\cdot \mathbf v}{|\mathbf v|^2}\).  That's correct.  So \(t_F = -\frac{2 (A - N)\cdot \mathbf v}{|\mathbf v|^2}\).

Now, if \((A - N)\cdot \mathbf v = -\frac{|\mathbf v|^2}{2}\), then \(t_F = 1\).  But we need to compute \((A - N)\cdot \mathbf v\).  Let's compute directly with fractions for the numeric example.

Given \(a = \sqrt{15}/4\), \(m = -1/4\), \(n = 7/4\), \(r = 1\), \(R = 2\).  Then \(P = (5/4, -15/(2\sqrt{15}))\).  Compute \(\mathbf v = P - A = (5/4, -15/(2\sqrt{15}) - \sqrt{15}/4)\).  Let's simplify \(p_y - a\):

\(p_y = -\frac{15}{2\sqrt{15}} = -\frac{\sqrt{15}}{2}\) because \(\frac{15}{\sqrt{15}} = \sqrt{15}\).  Indeed, \(15/\sqrt{15} = \sqrt{15}\).  So \(p_y = -\frac{\sqrt{15}}{2}\).  Then \(a = \frac{\sqrt{15}}{4}\).  So \(p_y - a = -\frac{\sqrt{15}}{2} - \frac{\sqrt{15}}{4} = -\frac{3\sqrt{15}}{4}\).

Thus \(\mathbf v = \left(\frac{5}{4}, -\frac{3\sqrt{15}}{4}\right)\).  Then \(|\mathbf v|^2 = \frac{25}{16} + \frac{9 \cdot 15}{16} = \frac{25 + 135}{16} = \frac{160}{16} = 10\).  Good.

Now compute \((A - N)\cdot \mathbf v\).  \(A - N = (0 - 7/4, a - 0) = (-7/4, \sqrt{15}/4)\).  Dot with \(\mathbf v\):

\[
(-7/4)*(5/4) + (\sqrt{15}/4)*(-3\sqrt{15}/4) = -\frac{35}{16} + \frac{-3 \cdot 15}{16} = -\frac{35}{16} - \frac{45}{16} = -\frac{80}{16} = -5.
\]

Thus \((A - N)\cdot \mathbf v = -5\).  Then \(t_F = -2 * (-5) / 10 = 1\).  So indeed \(t_F = 1\), which would make \(F = A + \mathbf v = P\).  But we earlier claimed that \(P\) is not on \(\Gamma\) because distance from \(N\) to \(P\) is not 2.  Let's compute that distance numerically with fractions:

\(N = (7/4, 0)\).  \(P = (5/4, -\sqrt{15}/2)\).  Difference: \(dx = 5/4 - 7/4 = -2/4 = -1/2\), \(dy = -\sqrt{15}/2 - 0 = -\sqrt{15}/2\).  Squared distance: \((1/2)^2 + (\sqrt{15}/2)^2 = 1/4 + 15/4 = 16/4 = 4\).  So distance is 2.  Indeed, \(P\) lies on \(\Gamma\)!  We earlier miscalculated because we used \(P = (1.25, -1.937)\) and \(N = (1.75, 0)\).  The distance squared was \((0.5)^2 + (1.937)^2 \approx 0.25 + 3.75 = 4\).  So indeed \(P\) is on \(\Gamma\).  That's interesting.  In our numeric, \(P\) is on both circles?  We have \(P\) is circumcenter of \(ACD\).  For our configuration, \(P\) ended up lying on \(\Gamma\) as well.  That seems to be a property: the circumcenter of \(ACD\) lies on \(\Gamma\).  Let's verify with the formulas: \(P\) is on \(\Gamma\) if \(|P - N|^2 = R^2\).  We have \(|P - N|^2 = ?\).  Using earlier relations, we can check if it's always true.  Indeed, from the derivation we have \(|\mathbf v|^2 = 2 r (r + n + R - m)\).  Also, we might find that \(|P - N|^2 = R^2\) holds.  Let's test with a generic numeric where we choose different numbers.  But in the O-centered system, we have \(A = (0,a)\), \(M = (m,0)\), \(N = (n,0)\).  Then \(C = (m - r, 0)\), \(D = (n + R, 0)\).  The circumcenter \(P\) we computed.  Is it always on \(\Gamma\)?  That would mean that \(NP = R\).  Let's compute \(|P - N|^2\) using our expressions.  We have \(P = (p_x, p_y)\).  Then

\[
|P - N|^2 = (p_x - n)^2 + p_y^2.
\]

We can try to see if this
